Children's Weekly in Spring and Autumn

The Attitude of Scientists 258

— Jun Peng

Little friends! We must know that this is a scientific world. A country without science will find it difficult to survive in this world. Who will create science for China? It is our little friends. Making ourselves into scientific children is also creating a scientific China.

Scientists are different from ordinary people. No matter what they encounter, they always maintain a questioning attitude: "Why is this so? How exactly does it work?" These questions constantly swirl in their minds, and they don't stop until they have thoroughly researched the matter!

Look! The American scientist Benjamin Franklin discovered the physics of white light reflection and black light absorption, and Isaac Newton invented the steam engine. I think you all know these stories. Both of these scientists were able to make these inventions because of these questions, discovering principles that ordinary people overlook.

Little friends! You should emulate the spirit of these two scientists, study nature, and strive to become scientists in the future. Hey! Little friends! Quickly take on the mission of creating a "scientific China."

Two Great Men Who Ranked Low in Exams 259

— Ou

Little friends, you have all participated in school or extracurricular exams, right? If you consistently rank at the top, naturally you deserve to be proud. But if you rank low, I advise you not to be discouraged. I'll tell you the exam stories of two great men:

Napoleon, the great French hero, took an arts and sciences award exam at the Lycée de Lyon, and he ranked fifteenth out of sixteen candidates. But he wasn't discouraged. He remained very self-confident, believing that he was second only to God. Later, he indeed achieved his great ambition.

Zhang Jian, the top scholar of the late Qing dynasty and a great industrialist in the Republic of China era, took the provincial exam at the age of fifteen, and he ranked beyond one hundredth. His teacher severely reprimanded him, saying, "If a thousand people take the exam, only one person will fail, and that person is you!" He felt very depressed and wrote the words "nine hundred ninety-nine" on his window frame and the top of his mosquito net to inspire himself to study hard. In the end, he did achieve the top rank in the empire.

The Founder of the Boy Scouts – British Lord Baden-Powell 260

— (Written by Dong Xun)

Fireflies 261

— Wang Cizhen

Tiny fireflies, lighting little lanterns; like little airplanes, soaring in the sky.

Tiny fireflies, with green fire glowing softly. Green little lightbulbs, the electric light never stops.

The Firefly Garden is in Yangzhou, a story left from the Sui Dynasty. Before electric lights were invented, there were only these childish games.

Emperor Yang of Sui had a Firefly Garden, and Che Yin had a firefly bag; one to help with diligent study, one to indulge in debauchery.

Fireflies are not formed from rotting grass; they have their own species. The end of their tails can emit light, a result of metabolism.

A Little Inventor 262

— Chen Shicong

Last time, I introduced a little friend who invented a telescope to you all. But this was accidental, and nothing special. Now I will introduce another little friend who made an invention through research to you all. I think everyone will be happy to hear about it.

This little inventor is German, named Webb, one year older than me—sixteen years old. He is a student. He had a scientific mind since he was a child and always wanted to invent something to contribute to the world. Others always laughed at him, but he was not discouraged by this. As the saying goes, where there is a will, there is a way. Recently, he invented a small electric boat and a wireless telegraph, and he can use wireless electricity to control the boat. The results are very good and he was commended by the government and praised by local people. Now he is preparing to build a larger boat that can carry people, still using wireless electricity to control it. It is expected that he will achieve considerable success.

Little friends, I hope that your thoughts and desires are like Webb's. Only then will China have a glimmer of hope.

How to Write a Diary 263

— Wang Shouqiu

Aren't there diaries in school? But those kinds of diaries are just not good enough! Not only are they the same few sentences every day, but the writing is also crooked, some characters big, some small. So writing that kind of diary for another year or two won't be of much use.

Does the above mean that diaries shouldn't be written at all? Of course that's not right. But I advocate paying attention to the following points when writing a diary: (1) The handwriting should be neat; (2) The narrative should be detailed; (3) It should not be interrupted for a single day. Originally, the function of writing a diary has three aspects: first, everything done each day is recorded, which can be used for reference in the future; second, it can practice calligraphy; third, it can practice composition; because there are these three benefits, the diary has become an indispensable task for everyone. However, the way of writing must not be as perfunctory as the school diary. If you write in that kind of stereotyped way, of course you won't receive the effectiveness of writing a diary!

I believe that if little friends over the age of ten can write a diary every day without interruption, until they graduate from middle school, then their grammar and calligraphy will definitely be very good. Little friends! I want you to start writing diaries seriously from today. Now, I will tell you again how to write a diary: (1) Date; (2) Weather; (if you wish to write the day of the week, you can write it before the weather); (3) Events; (choose the more valuable events of the day to write down); (4) Thoughts; (thoughts on a certain person or a certain thing).

Naughty Wang'er 264

— Jing Yuan

The police whistle was lost, and it turned out that Wang'er was stepping on it. Let's pick it up and play with it; "Qu qu..." Wang'er blew it frantically. The detectives thought they were chasing a thief, but pui! it was just this little rascal, making us panic!

Watermelon Lantern 265

— Lin Ling

We often see large piles of half-eaten watermelon rinds next to the garbage bins. We know that these things can be pickled in salt and dried to become very crisp and delicious snacks. However, we still don't know that these things can also be made into a very delicate toy.

When eating watermelon, we should cut the watermelon at two-thirds of the way. Scoop out the flesh of the one-third part, eat it and discard it. Then use a spoon to scoop out the flesh of the two-thirds part, scrape it clean, eat it, and then we can start making our toy - the watermelon lantern.

We use a spoon to scrape off as much as possible from the inside of the watermelon rind, wherever it can be scraped off. It should be as thin as possible, as long as the skin of the watermelon is not damaged. Then use a sharp knife to carve some landscapes, figures, or flowers and plants on the black outer layer of the watermelon rind. Here we should pay attention to the fact that every line must have the black outer layer of the watermelon rind scraped away. Otherwise, when a candle is lit inside the watermelon rind, the pattern on the outside will become blurry.

After we have carved the pattern on the watermelon rind, we drill a nail into the bottom center of the watermelon to prepare for inserting a candle. At the same time, we tie a thin rope or thick thread around the watermelon, and tie it to one end of a bamboo pole. In this way, when we lift the bamboo pole, the watermelon rind will follow. The watermelon lantern is finished.

In the evening, we insert a candle onto the nail in the watermelon rind, light it, and the pattern on the watermelon rind is clearly illuminated by the candlelight, thick and thin, while the unscraped parts are pitch black. We carry it and walk in the yard, street, field, or riverbank in the night. How interesting it is!

Slide 266

— Yi An

The Little Kingfisher's Wings 267

— Yi Zhen

The little kingfisher flapped its wings, sang a song, and flew out of its home, happily flying into the sky; when tired, it stopped on this tree and rested on that tree. It liked this kind of journey the most.

"Whoosh!" Suddenly, a bullet brushed past its ear, and its little wings were injured. It shouted and fell straight down, landing right in a pile of hay and hiding itself. Soon, people's footsteps passed by its ear. When it crawled out, it saw that its right wing had been pierced by a bullet, and blood was flowing non-stop, like a spring.

"Because of these hateful wings, I almost lost my life. Fortunately, I was alert. If I didn't have wings, the bullet would have just glided past my ear quietly, and there wouldn't have been this danger..." The little kingfisher was thinking when a fairy happened to pass by, so it requested:

"Kind fairy, I hate these wings. Please cut them off for me!"

"Really? You really don't want them?" the fairy said softly. "Will you regret it?"

"Really! I will never regret it!" The little kingfisher shook its head and said.

So the fairy took away the little kingfisher's wings.

Without its wings, the little kingfisher was much lighter and played in the wheat fields all day long, which was also comfortable.

One day, the little kingfisher was looking around idly on the edge of the field when it suddenly saw a child running with a bamboo pole. It immediately hid in the field, but the child refused to let go and kept chasing after it, hitting it with the bamboo pole. "Thwack!" It was hit on the forehead and fainted. When it woke up, it found itself sleeping in a cage and had lost its freedom.

"Alas! There is nothing superfluous in the world. If I had had two wings at the time, this imprisonment would never have happened." Thinking of this, it cried sadly.

Billiards 268

— Azalea

This is a very worthwhile thing to record. It's really strange! Ten out of ten children like billiards. Because it's easy to play, fun to play, and beneficial to physical health; therefore, children and billiards are simply inseparable day and night. They are very loving and good companions!

But unfortunately, things happen unexpectedly. For example, if several children are playing billiards and are in high spirits, suddenly the billiard ball is snatched by themselves or everyone and becomes defective, that is so boring; it bounces unevenly when played, jumping east and west, like an untamed wild horse, not willing to be controlled by itself! But it doesn't matter, you can buy some boiling water from the tiger stove and soak the billiard ball in the water. After a few minutes, you can find that the billiard ball's disease is cured.

Explanation: Because what is contained inside the billiard ball is air, and air cannot stand heat. Once heated, the body will gain weight and produce an expansion phenomenon. Curing billiard balls is using this little bit of physics.

Little Common Sense 269

— (Wang Qianchuo)

(1)

If an iron nail is nailed into a wooden board for too long, it will rust firmly. Sometimes, no matter how you dig or clamp it, it won't move at all. But if you nail the iron nail in a little further, and then dig or clamp it, it will be easier. This is because it has separated from the iron rust.

(2)

Little friends! If you are wearing new shoes (or very tight shoes), and someone accidentally steps on you while walking or exercising, wouldn't it be very troublesome if there is no shoehorn at that time? But at this time, you can use your handkerchief, because it is a simple shoehorn!

(3)

When we write with a fountain pen, the ink often spreads out after we erase it with a rubber eraser. But there is also a remedy for this, which is that after you erase it with a rubber eraser, use your fingernail to rub it to make the paper smoother. Then there will be no problem when you write again.

The Legend of Pinghu 270

— Mu Yin

Pinghu County was originally a town in Haiyan County, and its original name was Danghu Town. Later, due to its prosperity, the Ming Dynasty changed its name to Pinghu County and separated it from Haiyan County.

Little friends! I think many little friends must not know this history, so I will tell it here first. Now I want to tell you a folk legend of Pinghu.

Danghu Town was a very wealthy place during the Han Dynasty. The residents were always law-abiding and lived their happy lives. It is said that one day a general suddenly came there, wearing a military hat, military uniform, riding a white horse, and carrying a sword. He ran a big circle around Danghu Town; after running a circle, he stopped his horse and pointed his sword at the circle and said, "This place should be a lake." After he finished speaking, he turned around and ran away with a whip, but in the end, no one knew where he ran to.

Some residents who saw him at the time thought he was crazy and didn't care at all.

But on this night, there was suddenly a violent wind and rain, flying sand and rocks, which lasted all night. When everyone got up and opened the door the next day, they couldn't help but be surprised. It turned out that the circle that the man had circled yesterday had now turned into a lake! The people in that place were also buried and died in the water.

From then on, this place was called Danghu Town. But because its lake water was calm, it was called Pinghu.

Two Treasures 271

— Yan Biguang

Dear little friends! Do you know that we all have two treasures on us? If you don't know, please look at the following six sentences:

"Life has two treasures,

Hands and brain,

Think and do;

You can't eat it up in a lifetime,

Don't think and don't do;

You can't eat enough in a lifetime."

These are the words of the great educator Tao Xingzhi. It's really true. We are still in school now. When we go to society to do things in the future, we must keep the above sentences firmly in mind and use our hands and brains together. Then we can't eat it up in a lifetime. Otherwise, we can only watch others eat and use, and we will not eat enough in a lifetime.

The Word-Combining Picture of "National Salvation Through Aviation" 272

Avia-tion First, we must train aviation talents.

The Simplest Way to Catch Birds 273

— Linghu Zhao

Little friends, catching birds is indeed very interesting. Think about it, it would be so happy to catch a lively and singing little bird! But if we spend our precious time catching birds, it would be too uneconomical and too un-cost effective. Therefore, I will introduce you to a tried and tested economical method. Not only will you not waste much time, but you can also enjoy great fun. You little friends may want to try it to find out.

Tools: A shovel, a thicker wooden board, three thin bamboos and a little rice.

Instructions: First, choose a place where birds gather, and place the wooden board flat on the ground. Use the bamboo to draw a boundary line according to the wooden board, and then take a shovel and dig a soil pit with a depth of three and a half inches according to the line boundary (Figure 1). After digging, insert half of the bamboo head into the mud at the bottom of the pit; then take another bamboo and make it lean horizontally on the inserted end, see (Figure 2). Further, use the last thin bamboo to support it obliquely at the midpoint of the horizontally placed bamboo, see (Figure 3). After these three bamboos are properly placed, you can very carefully place the wooden board flat on the inclined bamboo head, see (Figure 4). Finally, sprinkle a handful of rice in the pit, and it is done! You only need to stand five or six feet away and watch the birds enter the pit, the wooden board will collapse, and you will be ready to catch them.

(Appendix) When the bird flies into the soil pit, it will definitely stand on the horizontal bamboo to peck for food. The horizontal bamboo cannot bear the pressure of the bird, so it will fall down, and the wooden board will also cover it. The bird is trapped in the pit. However, when you reach into the pit to catch it, you must be very careful, otherwise your efforts will be in vain and your joy will be empty.

Page 17

Women's World

Abortion 275

— Zi Jiu

"Abortion," in this world, is considered a crime everywhere except in the Soviet Union. Therefore, those who practice it have to do it secretly, and those who want an abortion have to do it even more secretly. Because it is done in secret, all kinds of problems arise. The newspapers of the 13th and 14th of this month all had reports of the Yu Yang abortion case in a legitimate hospital. The general idea is: "Mrs. Yu Yang, a boatwoman from Wuxi, because she disliked having too many children, came to Shanghai specifically to seek an abortion in a legitimate hospital. The two parties agreed on an abortion fee of 70 yuan, which included six pills, two bottles of liquid medicine, and two packets of powdered medicine. Mrs. Yang returned to the hotel and first took the pills, then the liquid medicine and powdered medicine. After five days, the fetal matter finally came out, but she was still in unbearable pain. In desperation, she sent someone to report to the Hongkou police station. The police station, on the grounds that abortion violated criminal law, brought the nurse—the doctor was on the run—the pregnant woman, and the fetal matter to the police station. The result of the trial was that Mrs. Yang was fined 80 yuan, and the nurse was released without charge..." From this news, one can also think of: it is often heard that a certain lady had an abortion in a certain hospital, costing hundreds of yuan, and a certain doctor specializes in secret abortions and makes a fortune. A certain woman sought a midwife's secret method for an abortion, and her life was buried. A certain lady took the so-called abortion elixir from a certain pharmacy, and the fetus did not come down and her whole body was swollen. A certain older sister took quinine to abort, and as a result, both ears became severely deaf. A certain sister-in-law privately took musk, and died from a massive hemorrhage, and other legends or facts. Rich people are being gouged by doctors, spending hundreds of yuan, which is not so important, but poor people have no access to treatment and have no choice but to seek midwives or medicines, and therefore lose their lives or become ill repeatedly. This is truly the most tragic and sorrowful thing in the world!

Examining the motives for wanting an abortion, they are roughly: (1) difficulty due to economic inability to educate and raise children, (2) enthusiasm for career, using this to reduce the trouble of raising children, (3) weak body, unable to withstand major childbirth, (4) pregnancy out of wedlock, fear of social slander, or no one to take responsibility for raising children, etc. But in this economic panic, in this current society where there is very little concern for the protection of children and women, we know that abortion will inevitably continue to flow and grow in the days to come. If we acknowledge that women and children are the pillars of humanity, it is necessary to urgently establish public, rational artificial abortion clinics or counseling centers. This is by no means advocating murder, but seeking happiness for humanity. Because rather than letting it do evil in secret, it is better to openly bring it into the right track. It is easier to manage and easier to monitor or restrict. As for the method, it is not within the scope of this article.

In addition, abortion is punishable by imprisonment under current Chinese law, which of course also needs to be researched and reformed. It is hoped that the current health administrators and legal scholars will pay attention to this.

The Soviet Wife (Continued, Part 3) 276

— By Anna Loviie Strong, Translated by Liang Qiu

What standards do Soviet wives use to judge chastity and divorce? They don't use traditional standards, only those of personality and social value. For us, the family is not separate and independent from the whole world; it is a unit of the world, and its value depends on its relationship to the whole world. This socialized way of measuring the family was crudely expressed in a conversation with a young glassworker. When I met him, he was recuperating at a sanatorium. One evening, he told me how he hoped to embrace a woman. Because he had previously expressed the same hope for an apple and a cigarette, I was a little offended by his words, and I was somewhat irritated.

"You seem to have many desires," I said, unintentionally implying strong desires. He angrily denied it: "My only desire is the revolution, the rest are just hopes." "Is a woman, like an apple, just one of your hopes?" I asked him. He said very frankly, "Of course, the hope for a woman is more serious, because it is related to the foundation of life and can affect the future. But even if a person is married, he cannot always be with his wife. This is also a temporary hope, which ends when it is satisfied. For me, there is only one permanent desire. That is to work with all my strength for the authority of the Soviets and to make the revolution penetrate the world."

"What about the woman in your desire?" I asked. "I hope she can be my comrade," he said indifferently, "otherwise, my feelings for her will not last."

Once, I lived in the same apartment as a twenty-year-old woman for a year. Several times I saw a young man who loved her spend the night in her room, and afterwards, I was surprised that she was still a virgin. She seemed very surprised at my surprise. She explained to me that the young man came to see her from another city, and because he had no place to live, he stayed with her, just like her girlfriends. "In our factory, almost every female worker is a virgin," she said. "Occasionally, there are two or three women who have casual relationships with men, but they are frivolous and do not work hard, and we despise them. Most women are afraid of having relationships with men." "Are they afraid for physiological reasons?" I asked her. "No, they are afraid of the consequences for us. A woman named Anna obviously changed after she got married. Although she did not leave the Youth Communist League, she did not neglect her work; but she lost her inherent interest and vitality. Perhaps she was pregnant, and her body was not as healthy as before. You see, a person's life can be so depressed; their interest in social undertakings can be so lost! This is the reason why we are afraid. We cannot pay too much attention to personal life before we have a solid social foundation." This attitude is understood by almost every unmarried woman in the Soviet Union, although most women are not so timid. Many young married couples are still studying at universities, the men living in male dormitories, the women living in female dormitories, and their children are placed in nurseries set up by the university. In this way, Soviet youth combine personal life and social responsibility. Therefore, personal "love" is not necessarily a threat to social interests; many people increase their interest in society because of it. But the ultimate goal of any of our marriages! Is not the mutual loyalty of the parties, but the mutual loyalty to social work.

Divorce, in the Soviet Union, happens as it does in other countries; but our morals regarding divorce are completely different from those in the rest of the world. In our country, any married person has the possibility of divorce at any time. Our legal theory believes that it is illegal to force a sexual union against a person's will. Many people divorce quietly, eliminating misunderstandings between them in a noble "agreement," which we believe is respectable and most reasonable, but which New York believes is the most immoral. In the United States, the two parties in a divorce publicly accuse each other in court of abuse or shameless behavior, which we see as despicable and rude. On the front page of a New York newspaper, it was reported that a husband sat outside his wife's room all winter night to watch her lover come out of her room. Our comment on this was: "A complete fool," or even crazy, spending the whole night in discomfort to find out things he didn't want to know! If he wanted his wife back, should he have done this? If he didn't want her back, why not forget the past sooner?" In our country, jealousy is not a praiseworthy virtue, but a remnant of cursed suffering.

X X X X X X

Powdering 277

— Bi Wu

It is rare for ordinary women to be as good as Yang Guifei of the Yang family. If the environment allows or encourages her to decorate herself, she will not "dislike the grease and powder for staining her color" and lightly sweep her eyebrows. In ancient times, in times of peace, men were refined and romantic, and women were light and charming. At this time, it was appropriate for women to do some makeup.

But in times of sorrow and mourning, like when the Northeast was initially lost three years ago, the whole country cried until their tears ran dry and their voices became hoarse, and women also looked haggard and disfigured. Even the most prosperous campus queen in the most prosperous Shanghai took off her bright clothes, and the so-called "blue cloth movement" became popular. This shows that everyone has the same patriotism in their hearts; when the environment does not allow them, women have not completely lost their conscience.

Time flies, carrying the painful past to the depths of the sea, bringing spring flowers and autumn moons, and painting a beautiful and happy world again. Gentlemen talk about Buddha and ghosts, about women and immortals; ladies put on lipstick and paint their eyebrows, oil their calves and dye their nails. There is a great atmosphere of peace, which can comfort some people who admire the ancients.

It's just that, if she occasionally looks at her heavily made-up self in the mirror and recalls the appearance of her blue cloth clothes three years ago, she secretly doesn't know whether to be happy or ashamed? In three years, the national crisis has not diminished slightly, but she has become like two different people before and after.

Some people compare our national crisis to a woman's childbirth; during childbirth, there is a burst of wailing and screaming, and after childbirth, she embraces her child with joy. This seems very appropriate at first glance, but it is actually irrelevant upon closer inspection. A woman giving birth to a child is creation, is new life; while a national crisis is a noose around the neck. If you must find a metaphor for the national crisis on women, I think it is best to compare it to a carbuncle. I once heard of a woman who had a carbuncle on her face. At first, she thought it was a freckle or a pimple, and covered it with thick grease and powder, thinking she could hide it, but she lost her life because of it.

The poison of the three-year national crisis has gradually deepened; but we are flowing into romance and beauty, grease and powder. It would be too strange not to be destroyed by this. Naturally, the enemy's cannons are indeed far away at this time; but taking this opportunity to create an atmosphere of peace, thinking that the world should be ours to talk and smile, and indulge in pleasure, this is truly a monster. I don't know how many women are sacrificed in this atmosphere. Using useful time for useless decoration; in the end, when disaster strikes, they think that the country was destroyed by those who dressed extravagantly. Fools only know how to float and sink with the tide, and even if they suffer the injustice of being wrongly accused, it is not a pity.

If women are not ignorant and look squarely at the current national crisis, will she only have the courage of the "blue cloth movement" three years ago, or will she have a more dignified attitude to correct the environment of grease and powder? What can be done to her?

Written before the third anniversary of "September 18th"

The Children's Nanny 278

— Xu Xingzhi

I often think of you,

Shizuko!

We only met once,

But you treated me like a confidant,

In front of the meeting hall veiled in drizzle,

You, holding the pillar, confided in me;

You asked me if I would hate Japan,

I said,

What hatred is there between people?

X X X X X X X X

I often think of you,

Shizuko!

We only talked once,

But you treated me like a companion,

On the fast-moving tram,

You, used a hairpin to prick out your address;

You asked me if I would like to associate with you,

I said,

I would like us to be friends from different countries.

X X X X X X X X

I often think of you,

Shizuko!

We only rode in the same car once,

But you treated me like a close friend,

You, live in a nursery for poor children,

Playing games with those children with a smile;

You asked me if I sympathized with these poor children,

I said,

Oh, I sympathize with them, and at the same time I also sympathize with their nanny.

On the Physiological and Lifestyle Influences of Female Writers 279

— Chen Junye

By a chance opportunity, I saw the Tianjin Yongbao newspaper of the 29th of last month at a friend's place. On another page of the supplement, I read an article titled "Comments on Japanese Female Writers," with the subtitle "Shifts in Thought Are Mostly Related to Physiology," which aroused my interest.

The first paragraph of this article reads: "Open a history of literature, and you won't see a woman's work called a masterpiece. This may be due to the social relations of the time. But now, even in the Soviet Union, you can't see a masterpiece like 'Virgin Soil Upturned.' This may be due to the physiological relationship of women. In China, there are only three or four female writers left; the rest have disappeared or died. But in neighboring Japan, female writers are developing... In advance, I discovered a surprising physiological influence, that is, female writers mostly accept the hints of their husbands. In physiology, after a woman has intercourse with a man, the man's qualities exist in the woman's blood, and in fact, her thoughts are also contaminated with many hints, such as Ding Ling being influenced by Hu Yepin, Kubokawa Inako being influenced by Kubokawa Tsurujiro, Nakajo being influenced by Miyamoto Kenji, and Hirabayashi Taiko being influenced by Kobori Jinji. This is a very obvious phenomenon."

From the above passage, we can easily see that the author of this article attributes the reason why female writers cannot produce masterpieces to physiological influences, which I think is very questionable.

First of all, I don't quite believe the sentence "Open a history of literature, and you won't see a woman's work called a masterpiece." The history of literature tells us that there are many good works produced by female writers. For example, to give just two examples, George Sand's pastoral novels in the French Romantic era are in no way inferior to male writers of the same era such as Alfred de Musset (in terms of artistic evaluation), is one example; the Soviet modern female writers Seifulina, Inber, and Shaginyan also have many successful works, which we must not obliterate. Speaking of Ding Ling in China, her novels have already been established and need not be explained here.

If we say that there have not been as many female writers as male writers in the history of literature, this statement is tenable. But the reason is not due to the physiological function of women. "After a woman has intercourse with a man, the man's qualities exist in the woman's blood..." and so on is completely insufficient to explain the reason why female writers are subordinate to men. The reason why there are fewer female writers than male writers in the history of literature must be attributed to the social reasons of the male-centered system. Taking our China as an example, in the past, women (even now) could not have much contact with social life at all, so it is of course difficult for them to demand the same literature as men. George Sand in France was a figure who betrayed the traditional ideas of the old society in thought and life, and her rich life enabled him to produce relatively considerable works, while Li Qingzhao in China could only write her melancholic poetry, which was also limited by her life. But in today's Soviet Union, the situation is very different. Seifulina and Shaginyan, as female workers, can produce amazing works, and the reason lies here, life comes first. (La Vie avant tout!)

As for saying that Ding Ling was influenced by Hu Yepin, Kubokawa Inako was influenced by Kubokawa Tsurujiro, and Nakajo was influenced by Miyamoto Kenji, it would be completely wrong to insist that this was due to their intercourse with their husbands. This statement may have been greatly influenced by Freud's poisonous thoughts! Rather than saying that this influence comes from the intercourse between the two parties, it is more likely that it comes from the mutual influence of habits and thoughts in their common life.

Regarding the failure of female writers to produce as rich creations as male writers, correct conclusions cannot be obtained from Freudian physiological explanations. There are already enough jokes made by Freudianism! If we want to find out the reasons why there are not many female writers and their works are not rich, we can only use historical materialism as the basis for our answer!

What Should We Do During the Transition Period? 280

—The Wise Mother and Good Wife System—

Editor:

After reading Mr. Li Hu's "Let Me Also Talk About Wise Mothers and Good Wives" and then Mr. Fei's "Who is Driving History Backwards," I couldn't help but have a very good feeling. I feel that Chinese people who pay attention to society are indeed more rational than before. They don't just yell based on their temporary feelings and ideals, regardless of the facts. Of course, there are exceptions, but it's much better!

I admire Mr. Fei's spirit of seeking "truth." He feels that men and women should have equal education and everything else equal for various reasons. That's right, as long as they are people, they should enjoy all equal rights! Mr. Fei's suggestion is good, "Why doesn't men's education embrace being a good husband and a wise father?" "Can women only be wise mothers and good wives?" But the question comes:

We don't approve of the "wise mother and good wife system," and of course we also oppose the good husband and wise father system. The same people should of course work for society equally and do their best to do social undertakings in society! However, in this way, what should we do with children and families? Although Mr. Fei stated, "This does not mean that men and women do not need 'cooperation,' 'assistance,' or do not raise and educate children..." But, under the mutual evasion of "wise mothers and good wives" and "good husbands and wise fathers," in addition to Mr. Liu Dabai's proposed "1. Organize public kitchens, 2. Establish public nurseries or public daycare centers," we have some doubts about the "disposal" of a group of children and families. What Mr. Fei said is in line with the ideal society. Before reaching the ideal society, of course we should not "refrain from eating for fear of choking." Should we be responsible for educating new children for those children who are mutually shirked? Should we have management responsibilities in the family, even if it is a very small matter? May I ask what Mr. Fei's ideal of cooperation, assistance, or raising and educating children is? Mr. Shao Lizi also said, "I absolutely agree with the issue of public childcare. I believe that when society is fundamentally transformed, this is an indispensable condition. If children are not raised publicly, labor issues and women's issues cannot be resolved." This shows that Mr. Shao Lizi "If children are not raised publicly, labor issues and women's issues cannot be resolved" focuses on "the fundamental transformation of society." What about the transition period? Should we ignore everything about the children, let them be, and not ask about the family, and concentrate on doing things in society and studying academics for society? The problem lies here.

In fact, Mr. Fei did not say that men and women should go to social groups at any time, and even more did not mention what should be done during the transition period. Mr. Fei's article "Who is Driving History Backwards" is just an article "Respectfully Questioning Mr. Li Hu." In this way, what I said above may be a bit "incongruous." But the serious problem is in the transition period. I think after Mr. Fei wrote "Who is Driving History Backwards," he should write another "Aftermath of Wise Mothers and Good Wives," otherwise the results advocated by Mr. Fei and Ms. Yunqi would be unimaginable!

As long as people with a little knowledge feel that the transition period is important. Mr. Sun Yat-sen emphasized the period of political tutelage in order to achieve the goal of constitutional government. If Mr. Fei and Ms. Yunqi are believers who support equality between men and women, then what attitude and methods should they adopt towards the current contradictory transition society? Are the previous proposals of the gentlemen feasible? Best wishes, Pan Yihong

Editor's Note: Since this magazine published Ms. Yunqi's article "Talking about the Wise Mother and Good Wife System," readers have sent in articles for discussion. Due to space limitations, we cannot publish them all. We had no choice but to select Mr. Li Hu's "Let Me Also Talk About the Wise Mother and Good Wife System" and publish it in the 29th issue of this magazine, and then publish Mr. Fei's article "Who is Driving History Backwards" in the 30th issue. Now, articles discussing this issue are still pouring in, including a letter from Mr. Pan Yihong, asking to find appropriate methods during this transition period. Now, in order to solicit readers' opinions and for the sake of public discussion, Mr. Pan's original letter is published here. Please readers express your opinions.

Girl Fisha 281

— Ding

Was it in the autumn six years ago?

When Fisha was still a young girl, her life was full of purity and enthusiasm. She had a pretty face, bright eyes, crescent eyebrows, cherry lips, and a dimpled smile. She was lively in nature and innocent in posture.

And her kind of organized speech, sensible, without the pedantry and restraint of old-fashioned family ladies, this aroused a kind of pride in her, or it can be said to be a reason for her self-esteem and arrogance.

Anyway, her kind of special quality aroused the pursuit and admiration of many men, as for women? Among her friends of the same sex, it can be said that eight or nine out of ten hated her, despised her, and envied her.

However, Fisha was completely a girl. She had a warm heart, and she seemed indifferent to those things.

Regarding her own future, she harbored a line of far-reaching hope. Her ideal was that there should be no distinction between women and men in terms of superiority or inferiority. She felt that women were no weaker than men. Indeed, in front of her, there were countless men kneeling at her skirt. She despised them. She hated those dull-witted guys. She looked down on a man who didn't look like a man at all.

Therefore, her vision expanded even more. She always hoped that she could become an outstanding woman, loved, praised, and admired by all the young men and women. She had an unusual temper, that is, she did not want, nor did she allow any men or women to have that kind of expression or behavior that despised her or disdained her. But she was not like ordinary women, who liked to be pretentious and shy in order to win people's favor. She often looked down on her own sex. She despised those frivolous women who were willing to degenerate and be played with. She felt that many women thought that they were not meant to be successful from birth, and that they were willing to be trampled on, but she would never admit this inferiority.

She liked to associate with men, wanting to absorb some fresh air in the atmosphere of the opposite sex, wanting to know a little more about the world, and learn some experiences and knowledge that were difficult to obtain among her own sex. She understood very well that spinning around in the circle of women all the time was of no benefit to her, but her interaction with men was not indiscriminate, nor did she mess around with people. She was determined to throw herself into the furnace of men and temper her. To cast and melt her personality, life, and physique, so that she can become a healthy human being. She knew that it was not enough to rely solely on the masculine, upright, and stubborn temperament, and it would not work to only have the feminine, gentle, and emotional aspect of women. A person, she felt, should have both kinds of temperament!

At first, when she was studying at a church school, needless to say, her thoughts were backward, stained with the smell of foreign slave education, the kind of thinking of a new-style bourgeois lady. She rebelled against the forms of feudal life, but she had no national consciousness.

Later, after leaving church school, her age gradually grew, and the contact with various figures in society made her gradually discover her own shortcomings. She felt great shame, great remorse, and disgust for her past erroneous words and deeds.

And one thing made her indignant, that is, among the women she had recently befriended, she was often ridiculed and scolded. She felt very uneasy in her heart. She felt that she was no worse than them. In ordinary worldly matters, she was confident that she was stronger than Jun Man, Qing Fen, and Ellie. How could she be insulted instead? Did they rely on some mysterious power to make her unable to resist?

Later, she gradually realized that her cleverness, arrogance, and that modern attitude were the biggest reasons for their aversion. This made her feel even more dissatisfied. Is it that their kind of simple, clumsy behavior should be praised? But no matter what, she always felt wronged, which made her distressed, made her depressed, and made her become angry. Telecommunications Special Issue

Special Issue of the Telecommunications Conference

Preface 282

— Lu Bing

The Telecommunications Conference was held from the 4th to the 6th of this month in the auditorium of the Ministry of Transportation in the capital. The attendees were numerous and orderly, and the results obtained were also very satisfactory. It can be said that it was an unprecedented grand event. The reporter participated in it and felt that the atmosphere of all parties was harmonious and amiable, and the opinions expressed were also sincere and sincere. Telecommunications includes radio and telephone. People may suspect that there are sectarian views, but if you try to carefully observe the content of the venue, you will find that it is a fusion of water and milk, and a cooperative effort. The development of the future of telecommunications can be said to have been fully grasped at this conference.

The reason why the Ministry of Transportation convened responsible personnel from the telecommunications departments of various provinces to hold a conference was mentioned by the reporter in the previous issue of this magazine. In recent years, although many policies have been implemented regarding the development of telecommunications services, the rectification and expansion of telecommunications lines, and the convenience of the public and increased efficiency, there are still regrets. Therefore, at this conference, the Ministry of Transportation sought detailed information on the situation in various places, extensively adopted many suggestions, and formed a practical and universal method, so that the situation gradually entered the right track, and the telecommunications industry could also advance with it. It cannot be compared with those who make high-sounding remarks and leave some impressions as material for post-event discussions.

Because of the satisfactory results of the conference, the harmonious feelings of all parties, and the promising development of the future of the industry, this magazine is happy to compile speeches, describe the actual situation, and issue it as a special issue. Readers who think about the importance of my country's telecommunications industry and look at this telecommunications conference can get a glimpse of the efforts of the transportation authorities.

Reading President Wang’s Address at the Telecommunications Policy Conference 283

— Zhen

The Telecommunications Policy Conference convened by the Ministry of Transportation has already opened on the 4th of this month. It is truly a grand event to gather talents together and broadly collect opinions from the public. At the time, President of the Executive Yuan, Mr. Wang Jingwei, graciously attended and delivered a speech of several thousand words. He incisively pointed out the reasons for the underdevelopment of telecommunications policy and the policies that should be adopted in the future, deeply hitting the current ills. After listening to the speech, the reporter couldn't help but feel a sense of solemn respect! The importance of Mr. Wang's address must be described:

Mr. Wang said, "Since the national crisis, among the various construction projects, the two ministries of Transportation and Railways have been striving for progress amidst the crisis and have achieved relatively good results. ... Postal and telecommunications, facing the same difficulties and suffering the same great losses, have, through the efforts and struggles of Minister Zhu and all responsible personnel, achieved their current results amidst the national crisis and other natural and man-made disasters." Since the September 18th Incident, among the state-run enterprises that have been hit, besides railways, postal and telecommunications have been the most affected. Taking telecommunications policy as an example, the losses included more than 230 reporting and telephone bureaus, more than 87,000 li of lines, and an annual loss of more than 3.1 million yuan in operating revenue. More than 3,000 colleagues were displaced and forced to live under the iron hooves of the puppet government, suffering the extreme pain of the world. However, to recover lost territory, it is essential to strengthen national power and work hard on construction. Based on the above sole objective, our transportation authorities have actively reorganized telecommunications policy. Significant achievements have been made in administrative reform, business improvement, engineering construction, and financial unification, which are a world apart from the chaotic situation of a few years ago. This process of struggling through difficulties gives us an important enlightenment: that telecommunications workers, under the guidance of the competent authorities, have doubled their efforts because they deeply realize that without promoting national consciousness, there is no way to talk about saving the nation and seeking survival; and without hard work on construction, there is no way to promote national consciousness. Is it not said that "national revival comes from many hardships"?

Mr. Wang also said, "Originally, the telecommunications industry is a very promising one, but since the Republic of China, the reason why it has not been fully developed is because it has been affected by military and political affairs. ... As a result, the future of telecommunications policy has been greatly affected and hit hard, all because the military and political organs do not understand that the telecommunications industry is commercial in nature." He also said, "The destruction by military and political organs should make them understand that the damage to state-run enterprises is also damage to their own interests." How deeply and painfully Mr. Wang spoke! Since the dynastic change, domestic politics has been unable to be unified, and conflicts over cities and land have been heard from time to time! The telecommunications industry has been almost completely destroyed as a result! Such as the abuse of military telegrams, the arbitrary appointment of bureau chiefs, the seizure of telecommunications funds, and the cutting of line poles, all of which have dealt fatal blows to telecommunications policy. Because domestic politics cannot be unified, the telecommunications industry cannot be developed. Because the telecommunications industry cannot be developed, domestic politics cannot be unified, the two being mutually cause and effect, and mutually related. Now that politics is gradually becoming clearer and telecommunications policy is making progress day by day, it can be seen from this Telecommunications Policy Conference that the heads of telecommunications policy from Guangdong, Guangxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou provinces have all come to the capital together to participate in the grand event. It can also be seen from the conference agenda that most of them focus on the overall plan for national telecommunications policy, and that unblocking remote communications is a matter of utmost urgency. From now on, national telecommunications policy has entered a unified period, and it is inevitable that the unification of telecommunications policy will promote the unification of politics. It is hoped that the military and political organs will deeply remember Mr. Wang's purpose, understand that telecommunications is commercial in nature, and also understand that destroying telecommunications is harming themselves. This should be given special attention by the military and political organs and the people of the whole country.

Finally, Mr. Wang put forward the policy of the Executive Yuan, which is "commercializing state-run enterprises," and the key to promoting this policy lies in "working together," which is a timeless argument today. State-run enterprises are most prone to bureaucratization. In the past few decades, telecommunications policy has been corrupted due to the influence of bureaucratic politics! To reform, it is necessary to implement commercialization. However, given the size of the country and the complexity of the telecommunications industry, it will not be successful without the concerted efforts of the whole country. In recent years, the telecommunications authorities have taken commercialization as the basis for telegram business, such as entrusting travel agencies to collect telegrams to facilitate telegrams for travelers; creating social telegrams to open up ways to use telegrams. Setting up business inspectors for liaison, adding proofreaders to avoid errors. Reducing the price of urgent telegrams, separately setting the charging method for the name and address of the recipient, exempting postage for telegrams forwarded by mail, and transit fees for telegrams forwarded by road, in order to reduce the cost of telegrams for the people, and the two methods of joint postal and telecommunications offices and merged bureaus and stations have the sole objective of saving expenses and facilitating the people. All these are policies of vigorous commercialization. As for the "working together" section, it is also a recent proposal of the Ministry. For example, the principle of entrusting provincial governments to handle long-distance telephones promulgated last year is the basis for cooperation with the provincial governments. This is in line with Mr. Wang's address.

Recalling the outbreak of the national crisis, Mr. Wang used "seeking unity through construction" as the slogan for saving the nation and seeking survival. For the past two years, Mr. Wang has been in charge of the country and has worked hard to realize it. At this Telecommunications Policy Conference, Mr. Wang delivered a speech with a sincere attitude. We should sincerely accept it, so as not to fail the great intention of our leader's eager desire for governance. In modern warfare, there is something called general mobilization, which means that under the supreme leader and the sole objective, everyone works hard on their own duties, and at the same time, everyone strengthens their national consciousness. This is where the telecommunications workers serve the country, and this is where they save themselves.

Answering Mr. Du He on the Matter of "Slow Telegrams Instead of Mail" 284

— Yuncheng

On the 6th of this month, the Shanghai News' New Garden published a conversation with Du He, the gist of which was that his younger brother, Yinwu, went to Guangzhou to attend the National Lawyers Association, and sent a telegram on the 31st of last month, but it was not received until 2:00 AM on the 2nd of this month, with an interval of 36 hours. (On the same day, the newspaper received a news telegram in only three hours). As a result, his whole family was very anxious. (Because the ship schedule would never be so slow). He wrote to the local telegraph office to inquire about this matter. According to the reply received by telephone, it seemed that the responsibility for the delay did not lie with the Shanghai Bureau, but with the Guangdong Bureau. But no matter which side delayed it, it can be seen that the situation of commercial telegrams being suppressed is still unavoidable. Although his matter is small, ordinary commercial telegrams are more important. If they are delayed for no reason, is it reasonable? Did this Telecommunications Policy Conference propose any methods to improve such a major shortcoming of "slow telegrams instead of mail"?

I am writing this article in response to Mr. Du He, not to defend the telegraph office, and even less to say that Mr. Du He's remarks are somewhat extreme. No - after reading Mr. Du He's remarks, I feel that he is indeed an old hand at talking for many years. Not only is it pleasant to listen to, but some places are indeed calm and very fair. For example, he said: "Since the establishment of the National Government, there seems to have been some progress in transportation administration in comparison." We express our great admiration for Mr. Du He's fair attitude. Because to be honest: the telegraph lines between Shanghai and South China have always been unable to be fully repaired and smooth due to political reasons. This is an open secret. If it were in the old days of warlords, it would be very common for a telegram from Guangzhou to Shanghai to take not only 36 hours, but even 72 hours or even 144 hours. Therefore, if it were in that era, a person like Mr. Du He who understands the situation would never be surprised. On the contrary, in countries with excellent and developed telecommunications in Europe and America, the speed of telegrams is measured in seconds. Then, if a news telegram from Guangzhou to Shanghai takes three hours, Mr. Du He may consider it satisfactory, but the people of that country must be as surprised as if it took 36 hours. Therefore, we not only do not feel disgusted by Mr. Du He's protest this time, but also feel that this is precisely the proof that the transportation authorities' efforts to improve telecommunications policy in recent years have achieved considerable results. To use a literary phrase, it can be said that "it is like the sound of footsteps in an empty valley," which makes people happy to hear.

However, although Mr. Du He is a giant in the literary world, he is still an outsider to the telegraph industry, so he is inevitably a bit misunderstood in his words. How do I know? Because he said, "Commercial telegrams are suppressed," and then said, "For no reason, they are delayed at will," as if the people in the telegraph office are all enemies with commercial telegrams, so they deliberately suppress them. He does not know that the income from commercial telegrams is the source of livelihood for the telegraph office staff. Commercial telegrams are their relatives, so why would they deliberately make things difficult for them! Then, Mr. Du He may ask, "Why does a news telegram from Guangzhou to Shanghai only take three hours, but my telegram takes 36 hours?" - Yes, please calm down, Mr. Du He, and let me explain it a little.

Originally, there are two wired circuits and one wireless circuit between Shanghai and Guangzhou. (In addition, there are two underwater lines from foreign companies, which connect Shanghai to Hong Kong and then to Guangzhou) The wireless circuit is direct, but its capacity is limited and cannot transmit all the telegrams between North China, Central China, and South China. One wired circuit is the near road along the coast, from Shanghai to Fuzhou, and from Fuzhou to Guangzhou. One is the long road that detours, from Shanghai to Hankou, Hankou to Changsha, Changsha to Hengzhou, Hengzhou to Shaoguan, and Shaoguan to Guangzhou. The news telegram mentioned by Mr. Du He probably took the wireless circuit, or even paid double the price to take the underwater line of a foreign company. And his brother's telegram took the near road of the coastal land line. Unfortunately, when this telegram just arrived in Fuzhou, the land line from Fuzhou to Shanghai was blocked due to irresistible reasons (everyone knows the reason), so it had to be returned and take the long road that detours. In this way, the time was inevitably delayed. At that time, the Guangzhou Telegraph Office did not send the telegram to the wireless station for transmission, which was a bit wrong. But we know that the transmission capacity of wireless is limited. If the wireless circuit was already very crowded at that time, it would be useless to send it over.

In short, I dare not say that the telegraph office is definitely not at fault in this matter - on this point, it is expected that the transportation authorities, which are known for their responsibility, will thoroughly investigate and give Mr. Du He a satisfactory answer. But even if the telegraph office is at fault, I can guarantee that it is definitely not intentional. Because the telegraph office relies on telegrams to make a living, just as the newspaper office relies on news to make a living. When newspapers publish news, it is sometimes inevitable that they are inaccurate due to insufficient coverage. If someone claims that the newspaper office specializes in spreading rumors based on this, I think Mr. Du He will definitely shout冤 (wāng) (to claim injustice) as well.

The Telecommunications Industry After the Telecommunications Policy Conference 285

The Characteristics of the Telecommunications Policy Conference 286

— Guosong

When the Telecommunications Policy Conference was about to open, the previous issue of this journal had already informed the people of the country of the three missions undertaken by the conference, namely, to discuss the implementation of plans, to sort out communication methods, and to study the improvement of business. Originally, the convocation of the conference was because the Minister of Transportation was eager to understand the telecommunications situation in various places in order to make overall plans and thoroughly rectify it. He specially invited the responsible personnel from various places to come to Nanjing to calmly discuss and gather public opinions widely for the reference of the Ministry. Therefore, the conference strived to minimize the scale and focused on implementation. It was neither a representative conference with restricted voting rights, nor a propaganda conference with external publicity. In other words, the conference was entirely an internal discussion and internal reorganization conference, so no reporters were present at the opening, and no declarations were issued at the closing.

Now, the Telecommunications Policy Conference opened on the 4th of this month, and the review, discussion and resolution were completed after three days, and it closed on the 6th. In total, there were more than 400 proposals at the conference. However, by summarizing them, they are nothing more than plans for the construction of wired, wireless and telephone circuits, the improvement of business operations, the training of personnel, and the reorganization of finance and the strengthening of the organization. Most of the resolutions were requested to be selected and implemented by the Ministry and Departments, because most of the proposals are principles and principles, and the specific measures are often vague. How to implement them, the value of deliberation and gains and losses is of great research value. The Telecommunications Department is the competent authority for telecommunications policy. It should carefully and thoroughly handle various proposals based on objective environment and factual basis, and distinguish between urgency and urgency, so that it is appropriate.

Some say: I have heard a lot about conferences. I still remember the Transportation Conference in the seventeenth year. How enthusiastic and great it was at that time! After the conference, there was silence, just like the end of the play, leaving only feelings. Can the Telecommunications Policy Conference be similar? I say: Not so! The spirit of the conference does not depend on the conference itself, but on the motivation and determination of the convener. The former Transportation Conference had a wide scope, the purpose was not specific, the personnel were involved, and the opinions were particularly complex. More proposals were about administration and less about technology. Therefore, the result was only the abolition of a Telecommunications Bureau, and there was no great contribution to the improvement of business operations, the design of projects. As for this Telecommunications Policy Conference, the Ministry of Transportation listened to the opinions of national experts as a reference for policy implementation, and at the same time informed them of the policies set by the Ministry and Departments, in order to achieve cooperation between the top and bottom. Emphasize implementation rather than empty talk, emphasize negotiation rather than eloquence, emphasize the development of the industry rather than the competition for rights. The motivation is pure, the goal is single, the determination is born of sincerity, and the conscience can be good. Success or failure, profits and losses, can be foreseen, which is not the same as the Transportation Conference. Is the spirit of the Telecommunications Policy Conference in this?

What I Saw at the Telecommunications Policy Conference 287

— Reporter

Since the National Government established its capital in Nanjing, various meetings have been held frequently. At the beginning, all the participants were excited and their blood was surging, thinking that various problems could be solved after the meeting. By the time of the opening, everyone was mostly perfunctory and irresponsible, or debated angrily and refused to yield to each other. After the closing, things passed, the situation changed, the smoke dissipated, and only a huge book of proposals was left for people to browse. Some people said that this kind of problem is due to the fact that the indolence of the Chinese people cannot be eradicated, others said that it is due to the fact that the Chinese people do not know the policies of the meeting, and others said that it is due to the fact that the competent authorities have no sincerity to implement it. Therefore, every meeting gives us a bad impression.

However, this Telecommunications Policy Conference cannot be viewed with the above prejudices. Because the motivation for the Ministry of Transportation to convene this meeting was to understand the situation in various places in order to make overall plans and thoroughly rectify it. Therefore, the purpose of the meeting was to invite national telecommunications experts to discuss and study together, so as to contribute various reform materials to the transportation authorities. Therefore, it does not emphasize form but emphasizes spirit, and does not advocate exclusive action but advocates cooperation. Between the members and the Ministry and Departments, there must be mutual trust between the top and bottom, and between the members and the members, there must be a harmonious relationship. There is no resentment, no disappointment, and no need for lobbying skills. Meet each other frankly and sincerely, this is the difference between the Telecommunications Policy Conference and various meetings.

Since the Telecommunications Policy Conference has special points, its results should have special achievements. What I can see, I write it on the left:

(1) The Spirit of Unity: According to the telecommunications industry, whether in terms of administration, technology, or business, it has a consistent nature as a whole, and there is no difference due to geographical relations and political changes. However, since the Republic of China, the telecommunications policy of our country has been affected by politics and military affairs, and it has been separated, disintegrated, and destroyed! The telecommunications reports of the southwestern provinces have not been reported to the central government for verification. Therefore, although the Ministry of Transportation has plans for overall calculation, it is difficult to implement. Because the telecommunications policy cannot be unified, there are many gaps in the political situation. Because of the gaps in the political situation, the telecommunications policy needs to be unified. At this Telecommunications Policy Conference, the heads of telecommunications policy from Guangdong, Guangxi, Sichuan, Yunnan, and Guizhou, the southwestern provinces, all arrived in Beijing on schedule to participate in the grand event. This is a major event in the history of telecommunications policy. After attending this meeting, the gentlemen from the southwest will report the actual situation in various places to the central government, and convey the central government's hard work in striving for governance to various places. The opinions of each other are close, and the spirit has become consistent. The unification of telecommunications policy is not far away.

(2) The Spirit of Cooperation: According to the construction of wireless telegraphs in our country began formally after the seventeenth year. Because the system is excellent and the equipment is perfect, domestic and foreign communications have considerable achievements and show their talents. At the same time, wired telecommunications is not willing to lag behind and is catching up quickly. In the past few years, the sound of wireless telecommunications conflicts has often shaken our ears. In fact, both wireless and wireless telecommunications have their own advantages and disadvantages. They should cooperate closely with each other and should not attack each other. This is the rational statement. However, the previous transportation authorities have no means to quickly cut through the mess, and have no attitude of holding upright and impartiality. Wireless telecommunications, although under the direct jurisdiction of the Ministry of Transportation, still exists in a confrontational situation. Since Minister Zhu took office, he has been honest, impartial, talented, and has spared no effort in reorganizing telecommunications policy. Therefore, in April this year, he resolutely merged the national bureaus and stations one by one. The disputes over the years have been cut off from now on, which is worthy of praise from the society. However, Zhu is still not satisfied with the current achievements. Therefore, at the opening, he earnestly instructed: "In the future, this Ministry must not only seek unity in telecommunications policy, but also seek close contact between postal, telecommunications, air, and aviation, so that they become a whole transportation industry that helps each other, and then extend to other state-run industries to form a piece." This sincere spirit of cooperation coincides with the spirit of working together of President Wang.

(3) The Spirit of Reform: The telecommunications policy of our country is seriously affected by national disasters, damaged by natural and man-made disasters, and the system is bad, the organization is empty, and the personnel is chaotic. Therefore, in the past fifty years, no significant development has been seen. In the past two years, the Vice Minister of Transportation has led from above, and the telecommunications colleagues have worked hard below to thoroughly reform the social reputation and is improving day by day. The Minister is still worried about the instability of the post, so he has formulated accounting systems and management regulations. He is also worried about the backward technology, so he has adopted new communication machinery, and held long-distance telephone and international telephone calls in nine provinces. He has high-sighted and foresight, and without the spirit of great fearlessness, he can achieve this! Also, looking at the proposals of the members, most of them are important plans to reform telecommunications policy. Wisdom is born of Ming, and knowing shame is courageous. The transportation authorities and the members know the shortcomings of telecommunications policy, and are ashamed of the backwardness of telecommunications, so they can propose reform plans and shake up the spirit of reform. All our colleagues should share this purpose, hold the final determination and the greatest perseverance, endure the burden, unite with one heart and one mind, and go to the merits and decrees. There is nothing that cannot be achieved.

The Telecommunications Policy Conference has already closed, and the grand plans will be implemented in order to satisfy the expectations of the people of the country. The reporter was fortunate to attend the event, and specially wrote down what he saw, and respectfully introduced it. Is it also a pleasure for the society to hear?
