Several Noteworthy Resolutions of the Telecommunications Policy Conference 289

— Qinghua

The Ministry of Transportation recently convened the Telecommunications Policy Conference. It is said that there were more than 400 proposals, most of which were related to the internal reorganization and improvement of telecommunications policy. There were also many related to the use of telecommunications by the people. The reporter will now report to the readers in summary:

1. Maintain the current telegram price: At this conference, many proposals were based on the fact that postal and railway prices have been increased repeatedly in recent years, suggesting that the price of inter-provincial telegrams should also be moderately increased by two or three cents per word to compensate for the losses of telecommunications policy. However, after the Ministry of Transportation explained the reasons why it was not convenient to increase the price, it was finally resolved to maintain the current price. This shows the Ministry's painstaking efforts to facilitate the people and not increase the burden on the people!

2. Charge double the ordinary rate for urgent long-distance calls. The urgent long-distance calls were originally charged at three times the ordinary rate. Now, in order to reduce the burden on the caller, it has been resolved to change to double the ordinary rate. In the future, those who have urgent matters to make long-distance calls can make full use of urgent calls, because it costs not much more than ordinary calls, and the calls can be very fast.

3. Increase the business hours of long-distance telephone bureaus: Some long-distance telephone bureaus in various places have very short business hours every day due to sluggish business, which is inconvenient for merchants and the people. Now, in order to facilitate merchants and the people to transmit business information in the morning and evening, it is specifically resolved to order the telephone bureaus to extend their business hours according to the actual situation of the local area, so as to benefit the business.

4. Specially made social telegram envelope newspapers: Social telegrams are mostly for congratulating on happy events or mourning funerals. According to the habits of the Chinese people, happy events are often in red, and funerals are in white or blue. If the telegram envelope and incoming newspaper of social telegrams are specially made with a kind of artistic and printed in color, and used for telegrams about congratulations, the recipient will be more happy, and the business will be easier to develop. Therefore, this proposal has also been passed, and it is expected that it will be realized soon.

5. Install automatic machines in radio stations in Shanghai, Tianjin, Xiamen, Fuzhou, Guangdong, etc.: There are a lot of telegrams to and from the above five places. Although there are telegraph bureaus, land and sea lines, and radio artificial wireless machines that can communicate, the land and sea lines are sometimes blocked. If all the reports are handed over to the radio station for transmission, the radio station will be difficult to handle because it is artificial telegraphing. Therefore, it was resolved at the meeting to promptly install high-speed automatic transmitting and receiving machines in each station, so that they can undertake a huge amount of reporting. In the future, after the official installation and communication, telegrams to and from Shanghai, North China, and South China will be very fast.

The above-mentioned resolutions will be prepared and implemented by the Ministry of Transportation in the shortest possible time. Readers should not mistake them as having been implemented.

Hopes Following the Postal and Telecommunications Conference 290

— Di You

The postal and telecommunications administration has been established for over fifty years, yet never before has a conference been convened to discuss improvement plans. Although the issue was touched upon during the Communications Conference in the seventeenth year of the Republic, its nature was not as specialized as this conference, and the proposals were not as numerous or substantial. Therefore, this conference marks a new record in the history of our nation's postal and telecommunications administration, and it is worthy of our commemoration, without a doubt.

The most emotionally stirring aspect of the conference was the arduous journeys undertaken by delegates from remote provinces, traveling great distances to attend. This not only proves that the previously fragmented postal and telecommunications administration has been restored to completeness, but also demonstrates that our nation is on the path to unification. However, amidst our joy and solace, everyone shares a painful sentiment—the absence of delegates from the four northeastern provinces! The postal and telecommunications administration of the four northeastern provinces, under Japanese control, has been transformed in ways unknown to us over the past three years. We hope that by the time of the next postal and telecommunications conference, the vast lost territories will have been recovered, and delegates from the Northeast will be able to attend. At that time, we will feel even greater genuine joy and solace. Therefore, I sincerely hope that all colleagues in the national postal and telecommunications administration will work together, diligently and tirelessly, under conditions of full cooperation, to shoulder our due responsibilities and jointly realize this great aspiration!

Secondly, since the founding of the Republic, the nation has faced many crises, and the postal and telecommunications administration has struggled precariously, constantly gasping for breath amidst hardship. It remains in dire straits today. The reason for this is naturally the decline in business, and the cause of the decline is the non-payment of fees for official military telegrams. According to statistics, official military telegram fees account for sixty percent of the national postal and telecommunications revenue. However, this majority percentage is merely a numerical representation; in reality, only one-tenth of these fees are actually collected in cash. The massive amount of official telegram fees owed from the era of the Beijing government need not be mentioned. Even since the establishment of the Nationalist Government in the seventeenth year of the Republic, the telegram fees owed by various military and political organizations amount to over twenty million yuan. How can the national postal and telecommunications agencies sustain themselves solely on the revenue from a small number of commercial telegrams? How can they avoid daily deterioration? The postal and telecommunications administration is now riddled with problems; without remedies, it will collapse beyond recovery. Currently, employees' salaries are in arrears and cannot be paid, shallow roads are neglected and cannot be repaired, and machinery is outdated and cannot be updated. Everything is truly unbearable to describe! In today's difficult circumstances for the government, it is understandable that political and military organizations cannot pay for telegrams, but many organizations have the means to pay in cash yet persist in the old habit of "never paying." If this mentality is not broken, the telecommunications industry will never find a solution.

Fortunately, Premier Wang's address clearly and thoroughly explained the situation with genuine sincerity, expressing the Executive Yuan's commitment to help. We are deeply grateful for this! We firmly believe that this wise leader will not only speak but also act, and will eradicate the aforementioned root causes one by one, allowing the postal and telecommunications administration to first achieve economic liberation, and then have the opportunity to improve and innovate. At the same time, we earnestly hope that all military and political authorities will abide by Premier Wang's wishes, understand the difficulties of the postal and telecommunications administration, and work together to promote the development of nationalized enterprises!

Reflections on the Closing of the Postal and Telecommunications Conference 291

— Hua

The highly anticipated Postal and Telecommunications Conference concluded in the capital on the sixth of this month, amidst widespread attention. Given the crucial importance of postal and telecommunications to the nation and society, the people's expectations for the conference were particularly high. The conference's mission was limited to discussing reforms in postal and telecommunications; how to implement the resolutions is within the purview of the authorities and beyond the conference's intervention. However, considering the communications authorities' efforts in recent years to improve postal and telecommunications, as well as their spirit of focusing on practical action rather than empty talk, one can anticipate that the conference will produce positive results. The fact that this conference did not focus on superficial pomp but instead dedicated itself to technical discussions, abandoning the long-standing bureaucratic habits, further confirms my words.

The implementation of government policies relies on the diligent execution of orders by lower-level personnel, but it also depends on the leaders' ability to supervise effectively to ensure practical results. In our nation's political circles, the observance of government orders has often been neglected, leading to the unfortunate consequence that laws and regulations become mere formalities, with a strange disconnect between laws and reality. The reason for this is largely the lack of effective supervision by leaders, although textual ambiguities or practical obstacles can also be major factors hindering the implementation of policies. The convening of this Postal and Telecommunications Conference brought together top officials and heads of affiliated agencies, allowing each to share their experiences in open discussions. The intentions of policies from higher-level authorities and the implementation processes of lower-level agencies could all be candidly presented and discussed, which will undoubtedly contribute significantly to the implementation of policies.

Furthermore, due to the number of participants, this conference was limited to the heads of key postal and telecommunications agencies. However, lower-level personnel, recognizing the importance of the conference, also submitted opinions in writing, requesting that the conference make public decisions. Although the attendees, due to the limited time, were unable to conduct detailed research, they still considered the interests of lower-level personnel and submitted the issues for discussion. This is particularly worthy of our praise.

Anecdotes from the Postal and Telecommunications Conference 292

— Lao Tan

The Postal and Telecommunications Conference lasted three days. Some noteworthy events occurred, and I will briefly recount what I saw to leave a trace.

Speeches by Several Important Figures—During the opening ceremony on September 4th, Minister of Communications Zhu Jiahua's speech was extremely sincere and moving, while Vice Minister Zhang Daofan's address contained many thought-provoking remarks. However, Premier Wang Jingwei was late due to attending a meeting of the Executive Yuan. The members present that day eagerly awaited to hear Premier Wang's insights, and his speech was met with frequent applause. Premier Wang is known nationwide for his eloquence, and the attendees were all satisfied with his elucidation of various points regarding the Postal and Telecommunications Conference.

Reporting Numbers at the Conference—Members were assigned numbers based on their order of registration, and seats were assigned accordingly. According to conference rules, each speaker should first report their number before speaking. However, some forgot to report their number and spoke directly, so the chairman often said, "Please report your number first." The conference recorders, by first listening to the number, could also identify the speaker, which greatly facilitated recording.

Distributed Publications at the Conference—The publications distributed at the conference included those from the International Telecommunication Union and reports on the postal and telecommunications industry in Zhejiang Province. They were distributed according to the assigned numbers and contained excellent content. This publication was also distributed to each member for their perusal.

Autodial 293

— Dun

The British Post Office has recently developed a device to be installed in automatic telephone subscribers' homes, allowing them to connect to the most frequently called numbers by simply pressing a lever, eliminating the need to dial the telephone number and repeated dial errors. This device is called the Autodial. The outside is a small box with a "needle," a "key," and "number holes." To make a call, the subscriber first inserts the needle into the desired number hole and then presses the key. This device is available in two versions, one with a capacity of twenty-five numbers and the other with a capacity of fifty numbers. The quarterly rental fee is only six shillings and eight shillings, respectively.

Shen Bao Local Supplement Amateur Weekly

Amateur Musings

Solemn Five Minutes 294

— Gong Pu

—Commemorating the Third Anniversary of the September 18th National Humiliation—

It is the third anniversary of "September 18th" again. National disasters are like family disasters, and the heads of families are always more deeply grieved than the children! Because as the head of a family, unless the family disaster is caused by unavoidable misfortunes, the head of the family bears a serious responsibility. On this day of heartache, the head of the family, seeing the scene, will naturally burst into tears, which is a common human emotion. The children, witnessing this tragic and mournful scene, have no intention of blaming past mistakes but only know to draw their swords and rise up, vowing to restore the family fortunes. This is as it should be. Otherwise, if everyone cries together, although it may be cathartic for a moment, when the tears are dry and the eyes are sore, facing each other blankly without any solutions, then the family will surely fall and the nation will surely perish.

The third anniversary of "September 18th" is a day of extreme national humiliation. Those in charge of national affairs have stipulated that on this day, "all banquets and entertainment nationwide shall cease, and party, government, military, police agencies, organizations, and schools in all localities shall hold commemorative gatherings. At 11:00 AM, work shall be suspended for five minutes, and everyone shall stand in silent contemplation, vowing to avenge the national humiliation, to express deep mourning." This shows how those in charge of national affairs are struggling for the nation, have not forgotten old hatreds, and want to use this day to cry for five minutes to release the grievances they have suffered as heads of families for the past few years. Their sadness and sorrow are deeply moving! But do the people, as children, still have the leisure at this time of national crisis to learn the lamentations of women and children, instead of becoming heroes drawing their swords to lead the nation forward?

Solemn commemorations cannot repel the enemy, and mere weeping is insufficient to restore the nation. During these five minutes of national silence, what should we silently contemplate in our minds?

First, we should thoroughly examine all the incorrect concepts and regrettable failures of the Chinese people's resistance to Japan since "September 18th," and recognize the true way forward.

Second, do not overlook the power of the people's resistance to Japan. The government should immediately engage in organizing the masses and forming a solid anti-Japanese front.

Third, we must prepare for self-defense, prepare for war against Japan, and prepare to recover lost territories with our own strength, opposing all imperialist activities of war within Chinese territory.

Fourth, we can no longer rely on anyone to fight our battles for us, and we must break the mentality of seeking temporary peace at any cost nationwide.

Fifth, we must eliminate the day of "September 18th," this extreme humiliation.

This year, we should not simply conclude matters with five minutes of sorrow, nor should we merely fulfill our national responsibilities with the above "conceptual" commemoration. I think that most of the readers of this publication, judging by their professional relationships, are merchants. I hope you can focus on boycotting Japanese goods for five minutes and act on it for a year.

We should restore the organizations that boycotted Japanese goods after September 18th, re-inspect Japanese goods, prohibit the sale of Japanese goods, and thoroughly investigate merchants who smuggle Japanese goods, change the trademarks of Japanese goods, and pass them off as domestic products. We should form an investigative network, densely distributed in various industries, to expose the conspiracies of traitors with the power of the masses. This is one way for our shop assistants and apprentices to draw their swords and become pioneers for the nation after these solemn five minutes.

We should all use our special social positions to commemorate "September 18th" with actions, and no longer simply "weep."

Current Affairs Research

The Future of Germany's Political Situation 295

— Yong De

—Domestic Political, Economic, and Diplomatic Difficulties—

We still remember last July 13, when Hitler reported to the National Socialist Party members in the Reichstag about the ins and outs of various Second Revolution conspiracy incidents, and received unanimous approval from all party members who shouted "Long live Hitler!" Since then, the foundation of Hitler's regime has become increasingly solid. At the same time, party members who were related to the Second Revolution conspiracy incidents were exiled, and close confidants were brought in, and this continues to this day.

Recently, President Hindenburg passed away. From an objective point of view, what will become of Hitler's regime in the future? Before raising this question, we must first recognize the important factors that can restrain the fate of Hitler's regime and the trends of various domestic political factors. There is an elite 100,000-man national defense force in Germany, and this 100,000-man national defense force has not yet been incited by the National Socialist Party's propaganda. They still maintain an independent position. This is a very obvious fact. The Sturmabteilung, known as Hitler's private army, has more than two million people and possesses great power, but it is now the only cancer of the National Socialist Party regime. In such a situation, what is the ultimate solution? Force the dissolution of the Sturmabteilung? Or completely reorganize the national defense force? This is the first major domestic political problem.

The second is the trend of public sentiment. The German masses are currently silent, like hibernating animals, but this cannot last forever. All freedom of speech and action is suppressed under authoritarian and dictatorial politics, and most of the masses do not trust the National Socialist Party regime at all. At the same time, there are many organizations of various opposition parties, and their ideas have deeply penetrated the people. On the other hand, power struggles and differences in political opinions among the National Socialist Party cadres make the future of the National Socialist Party regime, especially Hitler's regime, and its dictatorial rule, truly fraught with difficulties!

Third, there is the economic problem, which is closely related to domestic political issues. In terms of foreign trade, due to the increase in the value of the mark and the National Socialist Party government's xenophobic and self-sufficient trade policies, an anti-German sentiment has been aroused in various countries. Therefore, foreign trade has become increasingly sluggish recently. From January to May of this year, the import surplus reached 178 million marks. Comparing this figure with the export surplus of 263 million marks in the same period last year, the difference is clear. According to government announcements, the number of unemployed people has decreased by more than two million since Hitler came to power. On the surface, this must be said to be Hitler's achievement. But what is the actual situation? Although the number of unemployed people has decreased, the wages of all workers have sharply decreased. Therefore, although the number of unemployed workers has decreased, the total wages have instead decreased. In this contradictory situation, the workers are becoming increasingly impoverished. In addition, the soaring prices of necessities of life make it impossible for all the laboring classes to maintain their families, and they cannot even take care of their personal lives. In this way, the people's faith in Hitler's regime has become even more indifferent.

Finally, we must discuss the crisis in Germany's diplomatic relations. Since Germany withdrew from the League of Nations and the Disarmament Conference, it has become even more isolated in the international arena. In June of this year, Hitler's meeting with Mussolini was intended to promote friendly relations between Germany and Italy, and for a time there were rumors that Germany would break away from its isolated position and gain a powerful supporter. However, shortly after the two leaders met, the Austrian National Socialist Party assassinated Dollfuss in a rebellion. Respect for Austrian independence was the fundamental condition for friendly relations between Germany and Italy, and therefore, the Austrian coup event has led to an increasingly confrontational situation between Germany and Italy. This incident not only intensified the conflict between Germany and Italy, but also deepened the suspicion and antipathy of other countries toward Germany. The future diplomatic situation of Germany will become even more isolated, and this is undeniable.

When we examine Germany's domestic political problems, economic problems, and diplomatic problems, any element of any problem contains a major crisis. The National Socialist Party regime will be the tinderbox of a world war. In the past, Hitler said, "The National Socialist Party's world can continue for tens of millions of years!" But when we look at the situation described above, we dare not easily believe this statement!

Amateur Cafe

Father-Son Conflict 296

— Hui Qing

As long as contradictions among people have not been fundamentally eliminated, father-son conflicts will exist in every era. In China today, at a time when all contradictions are intensifying, these father-son conflicts are particularly widespread and acute. As long as we pay a little attention to the current social conditions and family phenomena in China, we can find examples of father-son conflicts everywhere. Fathers want to uphold traditional morality, but sons want to talk about modern fashion; fathers want stability, but sons want to be bold and decisive; fathers want conservatism, but sons want progress… Are not all these very common phenomena in Chinese society today?

However, how do these father-son conflicts arise? Volovsky, in his critique of Turgenev's "Fathers and Sons," said: "The two eras opposed to each other in Turgenev's novel are separated because they are, rather than one being the 'father' and the other the 'son,' representatives of two different social states that initially began the conflict. The roles of 'father' and 'son' only serve to sharpen the antagonistic relationship between two things." This is absolutely correct. Father-son conflict is not simply a father-son conflict, but the expression of the contradictions between two eras or two societies. Volovsky's statement is not only a correct comment on Turgenev's "Fathers and Sons," but also very suitable for critiquing the current phenomenon of father-son conflict in China.

Although the current situation in China is very complex, its main contradiction is expressed in the opposition between the old and new worlds, eras, or societies. Obviously, some people today have accepted an established traditional worldview in their life process, so they affirm reality and shake their heads at all the changes and new phenomena that arise from real life, considering them incredible. Conversely, other people, in their real life, under the constant stimulation of all the new changes produced by reality, are forced to embrace new "biases," deny established traditions, and stubbornly move forward on new paths. In addition to these, there are of course some people who live in between, or partially lean towards the former or the latter, but these people cannot exist independently and therefore cannot transcend the contradictions between the old and new worlds. Thus, the contradictions in Chinese society today are mainly the contradictions between the old and new worlds, eras, or societies. The so-called father-son conflict is mainly a reflection of this contradiction.

Of course, I am not saying that the contradictions between the old and new eras or societies are not expressed in any other situations besides father-son conflicts. No, I am not so foolish! I understand that the conflict between the old and the new is even more obvious in the struggles of the masses than in the father-son conflict; moreover, the father-son conflict can only be correctly explained in the struggles of the masses. However, when we discuss father-son conflict, saying that this conflict is mainly an expression of the contradictions between the old and new worldviews, saying that it is an expression of the contradictions between the old and new eras or societies, I am afraid there is nothing wrong with that.

Father-son conflict is, of course, the most unfortunate in the eyes of those moralists. Therefore, recently some people have followed these gentlemen's intentions and advocated resolving this problem as soon as possible. How to resolve it? They say: "There is no other way except for the father to yield to the son, or the son to yield to the father." However, the problem is not as simple as people think, and it cannot be solved by simply using two words.

We already know that father-son conflict mainly represents the contradiction between the old and new worldviews. If this contradiction cannot "yield" to each other, then the father-son conflict expressing this contradiction can absolutely not be resolved by "yielding." However, facts tell us that, throughout history, both ancient and modern, Chinese and foreign, the conflict between the old and new worlds has never been resolved by "yielding." The contradictions between the old and new forces in every era and every society are resolved in those contradictions. Specifically, they are resolved in the development process of the contradictions, due to the negation of the old forces by the new forces. Therefore, the father-son conflict, which mainly expresses the contradictions between the old and new worlds, eras, or societies, must be resolved in the development of this conflict. Those who want to alleviate this conflict by "yielding" will not have any significance other than expressing their fear of this conflict and attempting to hinder the evolution of human society promoted by this conflict.

The same is true when the problem is shifted to the current China. If father-son conflict is developing in China today, then this problem will inevitably be resolved in this development; moreover, this resolution will promote the progress of human society. If we are not afraid of progress, then there is no need to worry about this father-son conflict, and even less need to sing the praises of "yielding," calling for the son to "yield" to the father, or calling for the father to "yield" to the son.

Life

Customs Inspector 297

— Ru Yue

Because of the oppression of family finances and the panic of unemployment, I had to abandon the innocent and pure heart of my middle school days and desperately squeeze into this turbid society to find a job and solve the problem of making a living. I spent a lot of effort begging teachers, friends, and relatives to introduce and recommend me, and finally managed to get a position as an inspector in a customs inspection bureau hundreds of miles away from home, earning a salary of fifteen yuan a month.

The Customs Inspection Bureau is located in a prosperous county in the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. Upstream, it can reach Chongqing, and downstream, it can reach Yichang and Hankou. Merchant ships come and go every day. My job is to squat at the wharf, wait for the ships to arrive, and check whether there are smugglers carrying contraband and unscrupulous merchants who sell goods without paying taxes, or passengers and students carrying reactionary books.

The inspection work is easier when encountering ships going upstream than those going downstream, because the upstream ships have at least passed through one or two inspection agencies before reaching here, and we only need to search casually. However, ships going downstream to us are considered the first checkpoint (for example, ships departing from Chongqing have only undergone a very perfunctory inspection before raising anchor there), so our work is more troublesome and arduous. Firstly, because this place is a well-known export port for Sichuan soil and morphine, in order to evade taxes and seek advantages, merchants often smuggle goods out of Sichuan. Secondly, because the exchange rate for silver out of Sichuan province often requires a surcharge of about twenty or thirty yuan per hundred yuan, ordinary small merchants and students studying abroad like to carry cash (the outflow of cash is strictly prohibited by the provincial government). There is also the smuggling of Sichuan salt. Our inspection target is focused on opium, cash, and Sichuan salt. In recent years of economic panic and heavy taxes, almost everyone on the downstream ships, including some passengers, stewards, sailors, and cooks, likes to secretly carry some of these three things. Because there are too many of these villains, the inspection agencies have also become stricter, but no matter how strict you are, these criminals have never disappeared. The more strictly you inspect, the more ingenious and secret their methods of smuggling private goods become, and the more effort it takes to inspect. For example, take their hiding opium as an example. Some passengers make the luggage basket into a double-layered bottom, filling the empty frame between the two layers, which is two or three inches high, with opium. Even more ingenious is to use three or two small bamboo sticks, hollowing out the joints inside, rubbing the opium into noodles, inserting it into the bamboo, and then twisting the bamboo into the handle of the basket. Some also paste opium paste on the hanging axis of couplet calligraphy to blend in. The ones that are more ridiculous and ingenious than the previous ones are those who use pig urine bags to pack opium and hang them in the crotches of their pants inside menstrual belts on winter ships. There are too many things like this to tell. Because of their peculiar behavior, we have to work harder to discover their secrets. Therefore, as soon as the ship docks, we rush up like hunting dogs chasing wild rabbits, searching through boxes and baskets, carefully looking at every corner and every piece of luggage. When we encounter a basket, we have to poke it to the bottom with a wire, then take it out, smell it with our nose, and taste it with our mouth. We even have to ask everyone on the ship to take off their clothes for a search. Sometimes, when we see someone with a suspicious attitude, we have to feel her crotch to see if there is a pig urine bag containing opium or a fake menstrual belt there.

This tedious and painful work is of course despised and cursed, but since I have already eaten this bowl of rice, what else can I do if I don’t do this work that is despised and cursed? Moreover, according to the regulations of the bureau, every inspector must report at least one achievement per month (inspecting a batch of smuggled goods). If no achievement is reported for two consecutive months, there is a risk of losing the job. Because of this situation, how can I not endure the pain and fiercely

Continued on page five

Page 21

Page 22

Page 23

search people, extort people, and cause people to hate me!

I remember one winter, I didn't have any results for six consecutive weeks. The superiors thought that I had been bribed by merchants, passengers, and stewards, and gradually became dissatisfied with me. I realized this situation and became very anxious. Later, when a ship arrived, no matter who it was, I would ask them to take off their clothes for me to search. This time, I happened to encounter a middle-aged woman in steerage who was both cunning and vicious. When she took off her clothes for me to feel her purse, I don't know why my hand was a little too heavy and touched her body. She immediately slapped me a few times, followed by a few mouthfuls of saliva, and scolded me for deliberately pinching her breasts. But her saliva spat on my face, and the slaps hurt my heart. How should I seek justice? "Mountains don't fight with water, men don't fight with women." Should I fight back? Absolutely not. Finally, with a painful heart, I gently walked away amidst the laughter and sarcasm of the crowd.

People say: Customs Bureau inspectors have low salaries, but they are the most profitable positions. But I only feel that such inspectors are hateful and pitiful people in the world!

Naturally, under the pressure of superiors to do evil, and in the midst of a depressed and painful life, we are honed into a fierce nature and corrupt behavior. Isn't it true that, for example, when performing inspection duties, if anyone does not quickly open their boxes for us to see, or deliberately makes things difficult for us, then we will fiercely scold them, or even push them and kick them. In order to have achievements to report, and under the conditions of keeping our jobs and hoping for a salary increase, we often make an issue of things, and nitpick to seize small or even just suspicious items to punish passengers and detain stewards, etc. Speaking of corruption, when salaries are not paid for two or three months, in order to give gifts, entertain guests, etc., for our own depression and need for entertainment (naturally, we often have to play cards, drink alcohol, and visit prostitutes for recreation), or because the wives and children at home are waiting for money to be sent home for food and clothing, how can you not take the opportunity to extort, or openly let go and secretly accept bribes from smugglers to earn some "extra money"? Relying entirely on the salary? What is fifteen yuan enough for?

As for the noble and special passengers and their "precious family members," the inspectors have no way and no power to perform their inspection duties, although sometimes the contraband they carry may be hundreds of times more than that of ordinary passengers. If the inspector unwittingly disturbs the good dreams of those "precious family members," or even unintentionally finds something and "makes a scene" in public, then not only will your job be "taken away with a splash," but you will also become some kind of criminal.

Attention Unemployed Friends 298

A certain cultural institution wants to hire several field staff members. Those who have studied at secondary schools, have some knowledge of electricity, and can ride a bicycle are qualified. Those who are willing to apply, please send a detailed resume with a recent photo to Mr. Shi, 309 Bai'er Road, French Concession.

A certain school needs to add a female teacher to take charge of lower grades and teach music, physical education and other subjects. Those who are willing to take the job, please go to No. 3 Sanyuanfang, Yangshupu, to meet with Ms. Li.

A certain company needs to hire an English translator for documents. Those who are willing to take the job, please send a letter to Mengbo School, Belleri, Beller Road.

A certain primary school intends to hire a female teacher to teach music, drawing, and handicrafts. Those who are confident to be competent, please come to No. 12 Shendeli, at the intersection of Dongxi Huade Road and Gongping Road, Hongkou, to meet with Mr. Zhang.

A certain night school intends to hire a teacher. Those who are willing to take the job, please write a detailed resume and the amount of salary, and send it to Mr. Jia, No. 5 Beidi Fang, Beidi'ao Road.
